      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-number"><div class="field-content"><a href="#section-727" class="slidedown-trigger icon icon-plus">Section 16 (MSW)</a></div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title"><span class="field-content">‘Magnificent Diversity’: Eco-Thinking in the Age of Climate Change</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location"><div class="field-content">
<div class="field-section-time-location day-time">
    <div class="section-time">TUTH 12:00pm - 3:00pm</div></div>
</div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-last-name"><div class="field-content"><a href="/staff/teri-crisp">Teri Crisp</a></div></div>  
</div>

    
          
<div class="section-details slidedown-target views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets" id="section-727">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-ccn"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-ccn">Class Number: </strong><span class="field-content">13488</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-secion-time-location-1">Meeting time @ place: </strong><span class="field-content"><div class="field-section-time-location full">
    <div class="section-time">TUTH 12:00pm - 3:00pm @ L11 Unit 2 Towle</div></div>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-title-1">Section Theme: </strong><span class="field-content">‘Magnificent Diversity’: Eco-Thinking in the Age of Climate Change</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-nothing"><strong class="views-label views-label-nothing">Instructor: </strong><span class="field-content"><a href="/staff/teri-crisp">Teri Crisp</a></span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-body"><strong class="views-label views-label-body">Section Description: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>A hallmark of humanity is our extraordinary creativity, born and nurtured within the natural world. Yet human industry and development have resulted in the alarming loss of nature, accelerating in the last 150 years, along with climate change. What obligations do we have to other species, ecosystems, each other, and coming generations? How can wild nature be conserved or restored? What can industrialized peoples learn from traditional cultures? What can we learn from ‘eco-thinkers,’ past and present, whose vision has transcended the narrow confines of human-centered striving and conflict to embrace earth’s wonders? These are some of the questions we will pursue through reading a variety of writers (scientists, social thinkers, journalists, poets, activists, and others) and through films and art. And you will have the opportunity to develop your perspectives through writing and lively discussion. </p>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-book-list"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-book-list">Book List: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>(May change; please do not purchase in advance) <em>The Writer’s Diet: A Guide to Fit Prose</em> (Helen Sword), <em>A Modest Genius </em>(Hanne Strager), <em>Sharing the Earth</em> (Elizabeth Ammons), Course Reader.  </p>
</span></div>  
</div>

    </div>

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-ccn"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-ccn">Class Number: </strong><span class="field-content">44760</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-secion-time-location-1">Meeting time @ place: </strong><span class="field-content"><div class="field-section-time-location full">
    <div class="section-time">MW 9:00am - 12:00pm @ L20 Unit 1 Central</div></div>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-title-1">Section Theme: </strong><span class="field-content">Literatures of the African Diaspora</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-nothing"><strong class="views-label views-label-nothing">Instructor: </strong><span class="field-content"><a href="/staff/aparajita-nanda">Aparajita Nanda</a></span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-body"><strong class="views-label views-label-body">Section Description: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>The course material addresses the writings of the African diaspora in a broader definition of the term. It touches on specific themes and ideas from pre-colonial Nigeria to post-colonial Caribbean moving onto the “neo-colonial” New World. The course seeks to define the above terms as concepts and attitudes as exemplified in literature and films. This course focuses primarily on developing your critical thinking, reading and writing skills. It is the first in a two-course sequence that seeks to hone your techniques of expository writing. Basic rhetorical tools such as description, analysis, explanation, narration, speculation and argument are discussed enabling you to share your experiences, information and views with others.  The emphasis all along is on provocative theses, strategies of argument and competent analysis of evidence. </p>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-book-list"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-book-list">Book List: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>Author: Chinua Achebe  Title: Things Fall Apart, ISBN: 0-385-47454-7</p>
<p>Author: Jamaica Kincaid  Title: Annie John,​ ISBN: 0-374-52510-2</p>
<p>Author: Toni Morrison Title: Sula ISBN: 1-4000-3343-8</p>
</span></div>  
</div>

    </div>
  <div class="views-row views-row-10 views-row-even views-row-last slidedown-wrapper">
      
          
<div class="section-meta views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-number"><div class="field-content"><a href="#section-731" class="slidedown-trigger icon icon-plus">Section 20 </a></div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title"><span class="field-content">Madness in Culture</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location"><div class="field-content">
<div class="field-section-time-location day-time">
    <div class="section-time">MW 12:00pm - 3:00pm</div></div>
</div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-last-name"><div class="field-content"><a href="/staff/scott-wallin">Scott Wallin</a></div></div>  
</div>

    
          
<div class="section-details slidedown-target views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets" id="section-731">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-ccn"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-ccn">Class Number: </strong><span class="field-content">21859</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-secion-time-location-1">Meeting time @ place: </strong><span class="field-content"><div class="field-section-time-location full">
    <div class="section-time">MW 12:00pm - 3:00pm @ L20 Unit 1 Central</div></div>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-title-1">Section Theme: </strong><span class="field-content">Madness in Culture</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-nothing"><strong class="views-label views-label-nothing">Instructor: </strong><span class="field-content"><a href="/staff/scott-wallin">Scott Wallin</a></span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-body"><strong class="views-label views-label-body">Section Description: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>Psychiatry tells us that madness is “mental illness.” We may welcome this point of view when we are desperate to avoid suffering. But what are some of the other stories we tell? For example, what happens when we disagree whether someone is sick or not? Or when we explain the cause of madness in competing ways? Furthermore, not all madness is bad. Aristotle observes that “no excellent soul is exempt from a mixture of madness,” and some artistic work, such as Sarah Kane’s <em>4.48 Psychosis</em>, demonstrates its fecundity with stark beauty. Madness may entice us with its mystery, individuality, insight, or power. When we look at madness in culture, we see that it is not a simple, stable, objective medical condition but rather also a fluid social construction borne out of the stories we tell, the images we make, and the values we ascribe. Through your critical reading and writing about visual art, literature, films, theater, medicine, the law, and the news media, you will join these larger conversations and share your own responses, questions, and ideas on what it means to be mad and how we might think and feel about it.</p>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-book-list"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-book-list">Book List: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>Course Reader</p>
<p>Graff, Gerald &amp; Cathy Birkenstein. <em>"They Say/ I Say": The Moves That Matter in Academic Writing</em>, 2nd or 3rd edition (ISBN: 978-0-393-93584-4)</p>
<p>Kane, Sarah. <em>4.48 Psychosis </em>(ISBN: 0413748308)</p>
<p>Kesey, Ken. <em>One Flew Over the Cuckoo’s Nest</em> (ISBN: 978-0-143-12951-6)</p>
<p>Penhall, Joe. <em>Blue/Orange</em> (ISBN: 1408140918)</p>
</span></div>  
</div>

    </div>
    </div>

<article id="node-700" class="node node-ucb-course">
    <header>
                    <h2 class="node-title">CW R1A - Accelerated Reading and Composition</h2>
                <div class="course-offered">
            Fall 2017        </div>
    </header>


    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Description&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><p>This intensive, accelerated course satisfies concurrently the UC Entry Level Writing Requirement and the first half (Part A) of the Reading &amp; Composition Requirement. It offers students structured, sustained, and highly articulated practice in the recursive processes entailed in reading, critical analysis, and composing. Readings include imaginative, expository, and argumentative texts comparable in complexity to those encountered in the lower-division curriculum. Texts are chosen to represent views and perspectives of authors from diverse social and cultural backgrounds. Students read five thematically related book-length texts, or the equivalent, drawn from a range of genres, in addition to non-print sources. In response to these materials, they craft numerous short pieces leading up to three to five essays—works that include elements of narration, exposition, and argument. Students write a minimum of 40 pages of prose during this semester and they compose an annotated portfolio that showcases their best work.</p>
<p>Note: Specialized sections are available for multilingual student writers. These sections are marked (MSW) below.</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-available field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Available in&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Fall and Spring</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-prerequisites field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Prerequisites&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Placement by the Analytical Writing Placement Examination</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-units-format field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Units and Format&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">6 units – Six hours of lecture/discussion per week</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-coruse-grading field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Grading Option&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Must be taken for a letter grade for R&amp;C credit</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-fulfills field-type-taxonomy-term-reference field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Fulfills&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Reading &amp; Composition: 1st half (Part A)</div>
      </div>
</div>    </div> <!-- /content -->

    
            <div class="links">
                    </div> <!-- /links -->
    
    </article> <!-- /article #node -->    </div>

                            <div id="page-title">
                                        <h1>Access Denied</h1>
                                    </div>
            
            <section id="content">
                                    <div id="content-header">

                        
                        
                        
                                            </div>

<a href="/courses" class="back-link">All Courses</a>
<article id="node-696" class="node node-ucb-course">
    <header>
                    <h2 class="node-title">CW 1 - Grammar and Vocabulary of Written English</h2>
                <div class="course-offered">
            Fall 2017        </div>
    </header>


    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Description&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><p>This course develops students' ability to edit their own writing and to identify high-frequency, non-idiomatic uses of English. Intensive practice will be provided for students according to their individual needs.</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-available field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Available in&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Fall and Spring</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-prerequisites field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Prerequisites&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Self-selected non-native speakers of English</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-units-format field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Units and Format&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">2 units – Two hours of lecture per week</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-coruse-grading field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Grading Option&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Must be taken P/NP</div>
      </div>
</div>    </div> <!-- /content -->

    
            <div class="links">
                    </div> <!-- /links -->
    
    </article> <!-- /article #node -->    </div>

                <div id="content-area">
                    
                      <div class="region region-content">
    <div id="block-system-main" class="block block-system">

    <div class="content" >
        
<a href="/courses" class="back-link">All Courses</a>
<article id="node-704" class="node node-ucb-course">
    <header>
                    <h2 class="node-title">CW 131 - Introduction to the Craft of Creative Nonfiction</h2>
                <div class="course-offered">
            Fall 2017        </div>
    </header>


    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Description&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><p>This course in creative writing focuses on the craft of reading and writing creative nonfiction. The course provides an introduction to craft: how creative nonfiction is generated, what its elements are, and how finished pieces work. Students explore these aspects of craft through careful study of models by published writers, and through writing and revising their own short pieces.</p>
<p> </p>
</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-available field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Available in&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Fall</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-prerequisites field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Prerequisites&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Fulfillment of both halves (Parts A and B) of the Reading &amp; Composition Requirement or consent of instructor</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-units-format field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Units and Format&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">3 units – Three hours of lecture per week</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-coruse-grading field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Grading Option&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Letter grade</div>
      </div>
</div>    </div> <!-- /content -->

    
            <div class="links">
                    </div> <!-- /links -->
    
    </article> <!-- /article #node -->    </div>

    </div>
</div><div id="block-views-sections-sections_block_course" class="block block-views">
    <div class="block-inner">

            

    <div class="content" >
        <div class="view view-sections view-id-sections view-display-id-sections_block_course view-dom-id-2633c0c11c12a281933d65c556c40de4">
            <div class="view-header">
      <h2 class="section">Section</h2>
<h2 class="theme">Theme</h2>
<h2 class="time">Time</h2>
<h2 class="instructor">Instructor</h2>
    </div>
  
  
  
      <div class="view-content">
        <div class="views-row views-row-1 views-row-odd views-row-first views-row-last slidedown-wrapper">
      
          
<div class="section-meta views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-number"><div class="field-content"><a href="#section-764" class="slidedown-trigger icon icon-plus">Section 1 </a></div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title"><span class="field-content">Creative Nonfiction</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location"><div class="field-content">
<div class="field-section-time-location day-time">
    <div class="section-time">MWF 10:00am - 11:00am</div></div>
</div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-last-name"><div class="field-content"><a href="/staff/kaya-oakes">Kaya Oakes</a></div></div>  
</div>

    
          
<div class="section-details slidedown-target views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets" id="section-764">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-ccn"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-ccn">Class Number: </strong><span class="field-content">13472</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-secion-time-location-1">Meeting time @ place: </strong><span class="field-content"><div class="field-section-time-location full">
    <div class="section-time">MWF 10:00am - 11:00am @ 174 Barrows Hall</div></div>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-title-1">Section Theme: </strong><span class="field-content">Creative Nonfiction</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-nothing"><strong class="views-label views-label-nothing">Instructor: </strong><span class="field-content"><a href="/staff/kaya-oakes">Kaya Oakes</a></span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-body"><strong class="views-label views-label-body">Section Description: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>Creative nonfiction is the dominant literary form of our time. Over 2/3 of books on the best-seller list, in addition to thousands of essays in magazines, newspapers and blogs demonstrate the urgency of truth-telling today. The "creative" in creative nonfiction refers to craft rather than imagination: creative nonfiction uses literary techniques to engage readers in true stories. This course in creative writing focuses on the craft of reading and writing creative nonfiction. The course provides an introduction to craft: how creative nonfiction is generated, what its elements are, and how finished pieces work. Students explore these aspects of craft through careful study of models by published writers, and through writing and revising their own short pieces.</p>
<p>Over the course of the semester, you will write three creative nonfiction essays: a personal essay, a profile, and a researched nonfiction essay. Each essay will build off of short exercises and take into consideration literary techniques demonstrated in the books we will read. Because creative nonficton is a genre that's open to a vast variety of topics, this means students from all majors can use this class to learn how write about their passions and interests for a wide audience.</p>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-book-list"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-book-list">Book List: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>James Baldwin, Notes of A Native Son</p>
<p>Rebecca Solnit, Hope in the Dark</p>
<p>Joan Didion, The White Album</p>
<p>Phillip Lopate, The Art of the Personal Essay</p>
<p>Call and Kramer, Telling True Stories</p>
</span></div>  
</div>

    </div>
    </div>
  
  
  
  
  
  
</div>    </div>

    </div>
</div>  </div>

                                    </div>
            </section>

            
            
        </div>
    </div>

                                        <h1>Courses</h1>
                                    </div>
            
            <section id="content">
                                    <div id="content-header">

                <div id="content-area">
                    
                      <div class="region region-content">
    <div id="block-system-main" class="block block-system">
    <div class="block-inner">

            

    <div class="content" >
        
<a href="/courses" class="back-link">All Courses</a>
<article id="node-705" class="node node-ucb-course">
    <header>
                    <h2 class="node-title">CW 133 - Introduction to the Craft of Dramatic Writing</h2>
                <div class="course-offered">
            Fall 2017        </div>
    </header>


    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Description&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><p>This course in creative writing focuses on the fundamentals of reading and writing dramatic scripts. Students learn dramatic writing as an art and as a set of skills. They learn the elements involved in the creation of scripts by analyzing published scripts, as well as by drafting their own scripts and critiquing their peers' work. Particular emphasis is given to the work of generating and revising drafts, in addition to the critique and appreciation of works written for the stage, and to a lesser degree, for the screen. This introduction to craft is applicable to stage scripts as well as screenplays.</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-available field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Available in&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Fall and Spring</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-prerequisites field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Prerequisites&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Fulfillment of both halves (Parts A and B) of the Reading and Composition Requirement or consent of the instructor</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-units-format field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Units and Format&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">3 units – Three hours of lecture/discussion per week</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-coruse-grading field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Grading Option&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Letter grade or P/NP</div>
      </div>
</div>    </div> <!-- /content -->

    
            <div class="links">
                    </div> <!-- /links -->
    
    </article> <!-- /article #node -->    </div>

    </div>
</div><div id="block-views-sections-sections_block_course" class="block block-views">
    <div class="block-inner">

            

    <div class="content" >
        <div class="view view-sections view-id-sections view-display-id-sections_block_course view-dom-id-f6740bf490fd2471ef68f28830979443">
            <div class="view-header">
      <h2 class="section">Section</h2>
<h2 class="theme">Theme</h2>
<h2 class="time">Time</h2>
<h2 class="instructor">Instructor</h2>
    </div>
  
  
  
      <div class="view-content">
        <div class="views-row views-row-1 views-row-odd views-row-first views-row-last slidedown-wrapper">
      
          
<div class="section-meta views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-number"><div class="field-content"><a href="#section-765" class="slidedown-trigger icon icon-plus">Section 1 </a></div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title"><span class="field-content">None</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location"><div class="field-content">
<div class="field-section-time-location day-time">
    <div class="section-time">TUTH 3:30pm - 5:00pm</div></div>
</div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-last-name"><div class="field-content"><a href="/staff/john-levine">John Levine</a></div></div>  
</div>

    
          
<div class="section-details slidedown-target views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets" id="section-765">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-ccn"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-ccn">Class Number: </strong><span class="field-content">21809</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-secion-time-location-1">Meeting time @ place: </strong><span class="field-content"><div class="field-section-time-location full">
    <div class="section-time">TUTH 3:30pm - 5:00pm @ 187 Dwinelle Hall</div></div>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-title-1">Section Theme: </strong><span class="field-content">None</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-nothing"><strong class="views-label views-label-nothing">Instructor: </strong><span class="field-content"><a href="/staff/john-levine">John Levine</a></span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-body"><strong class="views-label views-label-body">Section Description: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>This course is an introduction to the craft of dramatic writing through the study of works by professional playwrights and through composition and revision of your own playscripts. You will come to understand dramatic writing as an art and as a set of skills; you will receive an introduction to some of the elements involved in the creation of written scripts. Particular emphasis will be given to the work of generating and revising writing, in addition to the critique and appreciation of works written for the stage and, to a lesser degree, for the screen.</p>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-book-list"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-book-list">Book List: </strong><span class="field-content"><p><em>Naked Playwriting</em> (Downs &amp; Russin), <em>The Poetics</em> (Aristotle), <em>This Is Our Youth</em> (Lonergan), <em>The Flick</em> (Baker), <em>Disgraced</em> (Akhtar)</p>
</span></div>  
</div>

    </div>
    </div>
  
  
  
  
  
  
</div>    </div>

    </div>
</div>  </div>

            </section>

<a href="/courses" class="back-link">All Courses</a>
<article id="node-697" class="node node-ucb-course">
    <header>
                    <h2 class="node-title">CW 10A - Introduction to Public Speaking</h2>
                <div class="course-offered">
            Fall 2017        </div>
    </header>


    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Description&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><p>This strictly introductory course presumes no formal training of any kind. Emphasis is on organization and delivery, with the goal of improving control over speaking habits and enunciation. A further goal is to introduce students to the foundation of rhetorical theory that underpins the practice of public speaking.</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-available field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Available in&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Fall and Spring</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-prerequisites field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Prerequisites&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">None</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-units-format field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Units and Format&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">3 units – Three hours of seminar/discussion per week</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-coruse-grading field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Grading Option&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Letter grade or P/NP</div>
      </div>
</div>    </div> <!-- /content -->

    
            <div class="links">
                    </div> <!-- /links -->
    
    </article> <!-- /article #node -->    </div>

<h2 class="theme">Theme</h2>
<h2 class="time">Time</h2>
<h2 class="instructor">Instructor</h2>
    </div>
  
  
  
      <div class="view-content">
        <div class="views-row views-row-1 views-row-odd views-row-first slidedown-wrapper">

<div class="field-section-time-location day-time">

<div class="section-details slidedown-target views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets" id="section-756">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-ccn"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-ccn">Class Number: </strong><span class="field-content">13555</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-secion-time-location-1">Meeting time @ place: </strong><span class="field-content"><div class="field-section-time-location full">
    <div class="section-time">MWF 11:00am - 12:00pm @ 104 Wheeler Hall</div></div>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-title-1">Section Theme: </strong><span class="field-content">None</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-nothing"><strong class="views-label views-label-nothing">Instructor: </strong><span class="field-content"><a href="/staff/mary-grover">Mary Grover</a></span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-body"><strong class="views-label views-label-body">Section Description: </strong><span class="field-content"></span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-book-list"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-book-list">Book List: </strong><span class="field-content"></span></div>  
</div>

    </div>
  <div class="views-row views-row-2 views-row-even slidedown-wrapper">
      
          
<div class="section-meta views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-number"><div class="field-content"><a href="#section-757" class="slidedown-trigger icon icon-plus">Section 2 </a></div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title"><span class="field-content">10A </span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location"><div class="field-content">
<div class="field-section-time-location day-time">
    <div class="section-time">TUTH 3:30pm - 5:00pm</div></div>
</div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-last-name"><div class="field-content"><a href="/staff/carolyn-hill">Carolyn Hill</a></div></div>  
</div>

    
          
<div class="section-details slidedown-target views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets" id="section-757">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-ccn"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-ccn">Class Number: </strong><span class="field-content">13556</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-secion-time-location-1">Meeting time @ place: </strong><span class="field-content"><div class="field-section-time-location full">
    <div class="section-time">TUTH 3:30pm - 5:00pm @ 228 Dwinelle Hall</div></div>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-title-1">Section Theme: </strong><span class="field-content">10A </span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-nothing"><strong class="views-label views-label-nothing">Instructor: </strong><span class="field-content"><a href="/staff/carolyn-hill">Carolyn Hill</a></span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-body"><strong class="views-label views-label-body">Section Description: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>How do you feel about speaking in public?  Are you petrified by fear?  Do you love the attention?  Do you wish people would listen to what you have to say? Maybe you want your audience to cry, to laugh, or to spring into action.  Maybe you want to sell a product, convey an idea, or get a job.  Maybe you just want to toast your best friend's wedding.  Sometime, somewhere, you're going to be standing in front of a bunch of strangers who are all waiting for you to open your mouth and dazzle them. This class will help you shine. </p>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-book-list"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-book-list">Book List: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>Lucas, Stephen E.  <em>The Art of Public Speaking</em>.  Boston: McGraw-Hill.  Any edition, including digital or very old used editions.</p>
</span></div>  
</div>

    </div>
  <div class="views-row views-row-3 views-row-odd views-row-last slidedown-wrapper">
      
          
<div class="section-meta views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-number"><div class="field-content"><a href="#section-758" class="slidedown-trigger icon icon-plus">Section 3 </a></div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title"><span class="field-content">None</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location"><div class="field-content">
<div class="field-section-time-location day-time">
    <div class="section-time">MWF 1:00pm - 2:00pm</div></div>
</div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-last-name"><div class="field-content"><a href="/staff/donnett-flash">Donnett Flash</a></div></div>  
</div>

    
          
<div class="section-details slidedown-target views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets" id="section-758">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-ccn"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-ccn">Class Number: </strong><span class="field-content">21863</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-secion-time-location-1">Meeting time @ place: </strong><span class="field-content"><div class="field-section-time-location full">
    <div class="section-time">MWF 1:00pm - 2:00pm @ 174 Barrows Hall</div></div>

                                        <h1>Courses</h1>
                                    </div>
            
            <section id="content">
                                    <div id="content-header">

                <div id="content-area">
                    
                      <div class="region region-content">
    <div id="block-system-main" class="block block-system">

    <div class="content" >
        
<a href="/courses" class="back-link">All Courses</a>
<article id="node-707" class="node node-ucb-course">
    <header>
                    <h2 class="node-title">CW 375 - Introduction to Teaching College Composition</h2>
                <div class="course-offered">
            Fall 2017        </div>
    </header>


    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Description&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><p>This course focuses on teaching philosophies, course designs, instructional methods, and assessment issues in relation to teaching composition in a pluralistic setting. CW 375 meets the campus policy requiring GSIs who teach Reading &amp; Composition courses to complete a semester-long, graduate-level pedagogy course.</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-available field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Available in&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Fall</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-prerequisites field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Prerequisites&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Appointment as a GSI or consent of instructor</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-units-format field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Units and Format&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">2 units – Two hours of lecture/discussion per week</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-coruse-grading field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Grading Option&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Must be taken S/U</div>
      </div>
</div>    </div> <!-- /content -->

    
            <div class="links">
                    </div> <!-- /links -->
    
    </article> <!-- /article #node -->    </div>

    </div>
</div><div id="block-views-sections-sections_block_course" class="block block-views">
    <div class="block-inner">

            

    <div class="content" >
        <div class="view view-sections view-id-sections view-display-id-sections_block_course view-dom-id-85cc51d902a64b57669bfcb0d3feef71">
            <div class="view-header">
      <h2 class="section">Section</h2>
<h2 class="theme">Theme</h2>
<h2 class="time">Time</h2>
<h2 class="instructor">Instructor</h2>
    </div>
  
  
  
      <div class="view-content">
        <div class="views-row views-row-1 views-row-odd views-row-first views-row-last slidedown-wrapper">
      
          
<div class="section-meta views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-number"><div class="field-content"><a href="#section-766" class="slidedown-trigger icon icon-plus">Section 1 </a></div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title"><span class="field-content">None</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location"><div class="field-content">
<div class="field-section-time-location day-time">
    <div class="section-time">W 4:00pm - 6:00pm</div></div>
</div></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-last-name"><div class="field-content"><a href="/staff/maggie-sokolik">Maggie Sokolik</a></div></div>  
</div>

    
          
<div class="section-details slidedown-target views-fieldset" data-module="views_fieldsets" id="section-766">

      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-ccn"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-ccn">Class Number: </strong><span class="field-content">13476</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-secion-time-location-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-secion-time-location-1">Meeting time @ place: </strong><span class="field-content"><div class="field-section-time-location full">
    <div class="section-time">W 4:00pm - 6:00pm @ 187 Dwinelle Hall</div></div>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-title-1"><strong class="views-label views-label-title-1">Section Theme: </strong><span class="field-content">None</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-nothing"><strong class="views-label views-label-nothing">Instructor: </strong><span class="field-content"><a href="/staff/maggie-sokolik">Maggie Sokolik</a></span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-body"><strong class="views-label views-label-body">Section Description: </strong><span class="field-content"><p>This course is designed to familiarize you with the major approaches and theoretical underpinnings relevant to the teaching reading and composition (R&amp;C) (or other fields involving writing) at the post-secondary level. We will review various topics in composition pedagogy, considering both theory and practice in the teaching of reading and writing.  </p>
<p>This course is 2 units, S/U, and restricted to graduate students with GSI appointments or who plan to have a GSI appointment.</p>
<p>We will focus on teaching philosophies, course designs, instructional methods, and assessment issues in relation to teaching composition with diverse populations.</p>
</span></div>      <div class="views-field views-field-field-section-book-list"><strong class="views-label views-label-field-section-book-list">Book List: </strong><span class="field-content"><p><em>The St. Martin’s Guide to Teaching Writing,</em> 7th Edition. C. Glenn &amp; M.A. Goldthwaite, Bedford-St. Martins, 2013. <br />Other readings,  provided through bCourses.</p>
</span></div>  
</div>

    </div>
    </div>
  
  
  
  
  
  
</div>    </div>

    </div>
</div>  </div>

            </section>

    <div class="content" >
        
<a href="/courses" class="back-link">All Courses</a>
<article id="node-698" class="node node-ucb-course">
    <header>
                    <h2 class="node-title">CW 25AC - Reading in and about US Education Institutions</h2>
                <div class="course-offered">
            Fall 2017        </div>
    </header>


    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Description&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><p>In this seminar, we will read, discuss, and write about the American educational system, especially within a multicultural context. The goal is to deepen the understanding of the history, diversity, and values of American educational institutions, while strengthening reading and seminar participation skills through synthesis, critique and analysis.</p>
<p>This course is partially intended to introduce international students to U.S. educational policy, debates, and history, but all students are welcome. The best class is one that allows for dialogue between internationally- and U.S.-educated students from diverse backgrounds. </p>
<p>Important: Although this class is offered by College Writing Programs, it is not a writing class. Students will, of course, do several short writing assignments, but class time will not be spent in discussing writing techniques, etc. Out-of-class conference times will be available for students who want to discuss their papers for the course. </p>
<p>In this course, students will:</p>
<ul><li>Broaden their understanding of the American educational system, especially in terms of socioeconomic class, race, and ethnicity.</li>
<li>Increase their awareness of the values that underlie and are reinforced by U.S. educational institutions</li>
<li>Improve their academic reading, presentation, group work, and discussion skills</li>
</ul><p>These aims will be addressed in the following ways:</p>
<ul><li>Reading of short articles, chapters, documents, and narratives exemplifying various educational/cultural ideas</li>
<li>Writing responses to readings, videos, and class discussion</li>
<li>Presenting on course materials</li>
<li>Conducting and reporting on outside research</li>
<li>Collaborating in teams to complete projects</li>
</ul><p>Breadth Requirement: This course satisfies the University's American Cultures Requirement</p>
<p>This course can be applied toward the Education Minor.</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-available field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Available in&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Fall and Spring</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-prerequisites field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Prerequisites&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">None</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-units-format field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Units and Format&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">3 units – Three hours of lecture per week</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-coruse-grading field-type-text field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Grading Option&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Letter grade or P/NP</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-course-fulfills field-type-taxonomy-term-reference field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Fulfills&nbsp;</div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Education Minor</div>
          <div class="field-item odd">American Cultures</div>
      </div>
</div>    </div> <!-- /content -->

                            <div id="page-title">
                                        <h1>Courses</h1>
                                    </div>
            
            <section id="content">
                                    <div id="content-header">

                        
                        
                        
                                            </div>
                

                <div id="content-area">
                    
                      <div class="region region-content">
    <div id="block-system-main" class="block block-system">
    <div class="block-inner">

            

    <div class="content" >
        <article id="node-18" class="node node-page">

            <header>
                                    <span property="dc:title" content="Courses" class="rdf-meta element-hidden"></span>
                    </header>
    
    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-field-introduction field-type-text-long field-label-hidden">
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even"><p>CWP does far more than administer the on-campus AWP Exam and teach the intensive, accelerated R1A that simultaneously satisfies the University's California Entry Level Writing Requirement and Composition Requirement. CWP offers a range of valuable and unique courses designed for students of all levels - from freshman to graduate students - that will suit your needs and interests and will help you effectively express your ideas and thoughtfully deploy your words.</p>
<p><a href="/file/395/download?token=cKi8o_L2" target="_blank">Fall 2017 class schedule [PDF]</a>  |  <a href="/file/422/download?token=E4d6jipb">Spring 2018 class schedule [PDF]</a></p>
<p><strong>View our <a href="/node/221">complete Course Catalog</a>.</strong></p>
</div>
      </div>
</div>    </div> <!-- /content -->

    
            <div class="links">
                    </div> <!-- /links -->
    
    </article> <!-- /article #node -->    </div>

<article id="node-156" class="node node-ucb-resource">

    <header>
                    <h2 class="node-title">Encouraging Student Writing </h2>
            </header>


    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-hidden">
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><p>This downloadable document provides information on how to help students improve their writing, including a series of "Tip Sheets" on writing for students, which may be duplicated and distributed. The tips are geared specifically for UC Berkeley instructors who assign writing in their courses, but who do not teach writing classes.</p>
<p></p><div class="media media-element-container media-default"><span class="file"><img class="file-icon" alt="PDF icon" title="application/pdf" src="/modules/file/icons/application-pdf.png" /><a href="/file/348/download?token=LD9uV3OO" type="application/pdf; length=1966132">Encouraging Student Writing</a> <span class="file-size">(1.88 MB)</span></span><div class="field field-name-field-file-type field-type-taxonomy-term-reference field-label-above">
      <div class="field-label">Type </div>
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even">Academic</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-file-description field-type-text-long field-label-hidden">
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even"><p>Information on how to help student improve their writing.</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div></div>
</div>
      </div>
</div>
    </div> <!-- /content -->

    <div class="content" >
        <a href="/resources" class="back-link">All Resources</a>

<article id="node-237" class="node node-ucb-resource node-sticky">

    <header>
                    <h2 class="node-title">Fair for Faculty Teaching Multilingual Students</h2>
            </header>


    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-hidden">
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><p>This information fair for faculty takes place annually on campus, offering advice and resources for teaching multingual and international students.  For handouts from past fairs, see the links to PDFs below.</p>
<p> </p>
<hr /><h3>Handouts and Resources from Previous Fairs</h3>
<p> </p>
<h4>Courses Offered<br /> </h4>
<p>A complete list of <a href="/node/221">all CWP courses</a></p>
<p>A list of <a href="/file/167/download?token=dUrLgstU">CWP courses for multilingual and international students</a></p>
<p> </p>
<h4>Berkeley’s Undergraduate Student Body<br /> </h4>
<p>15% of UC Berkeley undergraduates are international students.<br />25% of undergraduates are immigrant and/or US-born students who identify a language other than English as their native tongue.</p>
<p>Information about this diverse population:</p>
<p>PDF: <a href="/file/174/download?token=JhoXgDMB">Multilingual Student Writer Population</a> (2015)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/162/download?token=K_Ny3MjN">International Student Concerns and Programming</a> (2015)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/163/download?token=vaNLNztI">Working with F-1 and J-1 International Students</a> (2015)</p>
<p> </p>
<h4>Ways to Support Multilingual and International Students in Your Classes<br /> </h4>
<h5><strong>Encouraging Class Participation</strong></h5>
<p>PDF: <a href="/file/180/download?token=-fRjJAuQ">Participation Survey</a> (2014)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/171/download?token=FosD16ov">Encouraging Student Participation in the University Classroom</a> (2015)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/164/download?token=HMkuPfJr">17 Collaborative Learning Methods</a> (2015)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/165/download?token=_YKvjpxG">Collaborative Conferencing with Second-Language Writers</a> (2015)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/166/download?token=X7byjM9t">Improving Critical Reading</a> (2015)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/168/download?token=F0zt1pc5">Digital Tools for Students and Faculty</a> (2015)</p>
<p> </p>
<h5>Word Choice: <br />Why It’s So Complicated &amp; How to Support Students in Accurate Usage</h5>
<p>PDF: <a href="/file/176/download?token=wn2YD3mg">Word Choice and Vocabulary Development</a> (2015)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/177/download?token=HBXHVVwy">What You Need to Know about a Word to Use It Correctly in Your Writing</a> (2015)</p>
<p> </p>
<h5>Marking Grammar Errors in Student Writing:<br />What, When, Where, Why, and How</h5>
<p>PDF: <a href="/file/173/download?token=6H0JZskl">Marking Grammar Errors in Student Writing</a> (2015)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/175/download?token=cgGUt_RH">Editing Strategies to Share with Your Students</a> (2015)</p>
<p> </p>
<h5>Academic Honesty: <br />Giving Students the Tools to Avoid Unintentional Plagiarism</h5>
<p>PDF: <a href="/file/100/download?token=r4dmBbgW">Supporting Students' Understanding of Academic Honesty</a> (2014)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/101/download?token=Zy9mbwd9">Is it Paraphrasing, or Is It Plagiarism?</a> (2014)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/161/download?token=Je7iGD5M">Promoting Academic Honesty</a> (2015)</p>
<p> </p>
<h5>Publications &amp; Resources for Teaching Multilingual and International Students</h5>
<p>PDF: <a href="/file/102/download?token=LrCUR3jb">Resources for Faculty Teaching Multilingual and International Students</a> (2014)<br />PDF: <a href="/file/172/download?token=U8Fa2I6Q">General Resources for Faculty</a> (2015) <br />R&amp;C instructors may <a href="/resource/consultant-rc-instructors">schedule an appointment with CWP's consultant on teaching multilingual students</a>.</p>
<p> </p>
</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-field-resourse-person field-type-text field-label-above">

                            <div id="page-title">
                                        <h1>For Students</h1>
                                    </div>
            
            <section id="content">
                                    <div id="content-header">

                        
                        
                        
                                            </div>
                

                <div id="content-area">
                    
                      <div class="region region-content">
    <div id="block-system-main" class="block block-system">
    <div class="block-inner">

            

    <div class="content" >
        <article id="node-21" class="node node-page">

            <header>
                                    <span property="dc:title" content="For Students" class="rdf-meta element-hidden"></span>
                    </header>
    
    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-hidden">
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><h2>Requirements</h2>
<p>There are two writing requirements that students must satisfy to graduate. Both must be fulfilled by the end of the sophomore year.</p>
<ul><li>Entry-Level Writing</li>
<li>Reading &amp; Composition</li>
</ul><h2>AWP Exam</h2>
<p>The Analytical Writing Placement Exam (AWPE) enables students to demonstrate proficiency in reading and writing at the college entry level.</p>
<h2>Academic Honesty</h2>
<p>The University upholds a code of student conduct and the College Writing Programs supports that code through its position on plagiarism and acts of academic dishonesty and conventions for ethical citation.</p>
<p> </p>
</div>
      </div>
</div>    </div> <!-- /content -->

    <div id="main" class="clearfix" role="main">
        <div class="container">
                            <div id="page-title">
                                        <h1>Academic Honesty</h1>
                                    </div>
            
            <section id="content">
                                    <div id="content-header">

                        
                        
                        
                                            </div>
                

                <div id="content-area">
                    
                      <div class="region region-content">
    <div id="block-system-main" class="block block-system">
    <div class="block-inner">

            

    <div class="content" >
        <article id="node-81" class="node node-page">

            <header>
                                    <span property="dc:title" content="Academic Honesty" class="rdf-meta element-hidden"></span>
                    </header>
    
    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-field-introduction field-type-text-long field-label-hidden">
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even"><p>The College Writing Program has a zero-tolerance policy regarding plagiarism. Students who submit plagiarized work will be subject to consequences ranging from a grade of "F" on the assignment to suspension from the University. For more on academic dishonesty and its consequences, see the <a class="external-link" href="http://sa.berkeley.edu/student-code-of-conduct" target="_blank">Code of Student Conduct</a>.</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-hidden">
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><h2>Plagiarism</h2>
<p>The Center for Student Conduct offers the following <a class="external-link" href="http://sa.berkeley.edu/conduct/integrity/definition" target="_blank">definition of plagiarism</a>:</p>
<p>"Plagiarism is defined as use of intellectual material produced by another person without acknowledging its source, for example:</p>
<ul><li>Wholesale copying of passages from works of others into your homework, essay, term paper, or dissertation without acknowledgment.</li>
<li>Use of the views, opinions, or insights of another without acknowledgment.</li>
<li>Paraphrasing of another person's characteristic or original phraseology, metaphor, or other literary device without acknowledgment."</li>
</ul><h2>Consequences</h2>
<p>The Berkeley Academic Guide states the following about <a class="external-link" href="http://guide.berkeley.edu/academic-policies/#studentconductappealstext" target="_blank">plagiarism and its disciplinary consequences</a>:</p>
<p>"Achievement and proficiency in subject matter include your realization that neither is to be achieved by cheating. An instructor has the right to give you an F on a single assignment produced by cheating without determining whether you have a passing knowledge of the relevant factual material. That is an appropriate academic evaluation for a failure to understand or abide by the basic rules of academic study and inquiry. An instructor has the right to assign a final grade of F for the course if you plagiarized a paper for a portion of the course, even if you have successfully and, presumably, honestly passed the remaining portion of the course. It must be understood that any student who knowingly aids in plagiarism or other cheating, e.g., allowing another student to copy a paper or examination question, is as guilty as the cheating student."</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div>    </div> <!-- /content -->

    
            <div class="links">
                    </div> <!-- /links -->
    
    </article> <!-- /article #node -->    </div>

    </div>
</div>  </div>

                                    </div>
            </section>

    <div id="main" class="clearfix" role="main">
        <div class="container">
                            <div id="page-title">
                                        <h1>AWP Exam</h1>
                                    </div>
            
            <section id="content">
                                    <div id="content-header">

                        
                        
                        
                                            </div>
                

                <div id="content-area">
                    
                      <div class="region region-content">
    <div id="block-system-main" class="block block-system">
    <div class="block-inner">

            

    <div class="content" >
        <article id="node-79" class="node node-page">

            <header>
                                    <span property="dc:title" content="AWP Exam" class="rdf-meta element-hidden"></span>
                    </header>
    
    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-field-introduction field-type-text-long field-label-hidden">
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even"><p>The AWPE is administered to college-bound high school seniors each May at testing centers across the state of California. </p>
<p>The AWPE is also administered on campus for those who did not attend high school in California, or who were otherwise unable to take the May exam. Campus exams are administered in September and February.</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-hidden">
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><p>For more information, see the <a class="external-link" href="http://www.ucop.edu/elwr/index.html" target="_blank">Analytical Writing Placement Examination</a> website.</p>
<p>A fee is required to take the exam. The <a class="external-link" href="https://www.awpe.org/" target="_blank">fee can only be paid online</a>.</p>
<p>The Analytical Writing Placement Examination provides students with a prose passage of some 700 to 1,000 words. This passage concerns an issue accessible to all freshmen, although it may include some perspectives or information that will be new to them. The passage is of the level of difficulty encountered in beginning university courses, and may be drawn from any of a number of disciplines. Frequently it presents a point of view with which there can clearly be disagreement — a viewpoint, that is, about a truly arguable issue.  After reading the passage, students write an essay responding to a single topic based on the passage's content.<br /> </p>
<h2>Campus Examination</h2>
<p>If students have been admitted to UC Berkeley but have not yet fulfilled the University of California Entry-Level Writing Requirement or taken the Analytical Writing Placement Examination, they should take the exam during their first semester at Berkeley. A fee is required to take the exam.</p>
<p>Students must visit the fee <a class="external-link" href="https://www.awpe.org" target="_blank">payment / fee waiver</a> website, Follow the instructions to pay the AWPE fee or confirm that the fee has been waived, and print the Payment Status page.  All students must bring their printed Payment Status to the exam.</p>
<p>In Spring 2018, the Berkeley campus Analytical Writing Placement Examination will be held:</p>
<p style="margin-left: 40px;"><strong>Saturday, February 24, 2018 10:00 am - 12:00 noon, Room to be announced.</strong><br /><em>To be admitted, students must bring their student ID, a pen, and their printed Payment Status page.</em> Exams written in pencil will not be accepted.</p>
<p>Results will be available approximately three weeks after the exam is administered. For more information, <a href="/form/contact-us">contact us</a>.</p>
<h3>Frequently Asked Questions</h3>
<p>If you have questions about the AWP Exam, <a href="/about-us/faq">please see our FAQs</a>. If you don’t find your questions answered there, <a href="/form/contact-us">contact us</a>.</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div>    </div> <!-- /content -->

    
            <div class="links">
                    </div> <!-- /links -->
    
    </article> <!-- /article #node -->    </div>

    </div>
</div>  </div>

            </section>

    <div id="main" class="clearfix" role="main">
        <div class="container">
                            <div id="page-title">
                                        <h1>Requirements</h1>
                                    </div>
            
            <section id="content">
                                    <div id="content-header">

                        
                        
                        
                                            </div>
                

                <div id="content-area">
                    
                      <div class="region region-content">
    <div id="block-system-main" class="block block-system">
    <div class="block-inner">

            

    <div class="content" >
        <article id="node-78" class="node node-page">

            <header>
                                    <span property="dc:title" content="Requirements" class="rdf-meta element-hidden"></span>
                    </header>
    
    <div class="content">
        <div class="field field-name-field-introduction field-type-text-long field-label-hidden">
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even"><p>There are two writing requirements that students must satisfy to graduate: Entry-Level Writing, and Reading &amp; Composition.</p>
<p>In addition to courses that satisfy the Reading &amp; Composition requirement, CWP offers courses that satisfy various other requirements.</p>
</div>
      </div>
</div><div class="field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-hidden">
    <div class="field-items">
          <div class="field-item even" property="content:encoded"><h2>Entry-Level Writing</h2>
<p>The UC Entry-Level Writing requirement is a Universitywide writing requirement. All students entering the University of California as freshmen must demonstrate their command of the English language by fulfilling this requirement. Fulfillment of this requirement is a prerequisite to enrolling in all Reading &amp; Composition courses except for College Writing R1A.</p>
<p>There are two ways to satisfy the requirement, by coursework or by exam, and it depends on whether or not you have started classes at Berkeley. </p>
<h3>If you have not started classes at Berkeley</h3>
<p>To meet this requirement by <strong>exam</strong> before you have started classes at Berkeley, you must score</p>
<ul><li>30 or above on the ACT English Language Arts test; or</li>
<li>30 or above on the ACT Combined English/Writing test (taken June 2015 or earlier); or</li>
<li>680 or above on the College Board SAT Reasoning Test--Writing Section (taken January 2016 or earlier); or</li>
<li>3 or above on the Advanced Placement Examination in English Language and Composition; or </li>
<li>3 or above on the Advanced Placement Examination in English Literature and Composition; or </li>
<li>5 or above on the International Baccalaureate Higher Level English A: Literature exam (formerly known as Higher Level English A1 exam); or</li>
<li>6 or above on the International Baccalaureate Standard Level English A: Literature exam (formerly known as Standard Level English A1 exam) ; or</li>
<li>5 or above on the International Baccalaureate Higher Level English A: Language and Literature exam; or</li>
<li>6 or above on the International Baccalaureate Standard Level English A: Language and Literature exam, or</li>
<li>8 or above on the Analytical Writing Placement Examination taken at your high school's exam center.</li>
</ul><p>To meet this requirement by <strong>coursework</strong>, you must earn a grade of C or higher in a college course certified by UC Berkeley as satisfying the Entry-Level Writing Requirement.</p>
<h3>If you have started classes at Berkeley</h3>
<p>To meet this requirement by <strong>exam</strong> after you have started classes at Berkeley, you must score 8 or above on the Analytical Writing Placement Examination taken on the Berkeley campus.</p>
<p>To meet this requirement by <strong>coursework</strong>, you must earn a grade of C or higher in College Writing R1A.</p>
<h2><br />Reading &amp; Composition </h2>
<p>The Reading &amp; Composition requirement is a two-part sequence required of Berkeley undergraduates at the lower-division level to provide them with a solid foundation in reading, writing, and critical thinking for work in the major and beyond.</p>
<p>All undergraduates must complete the R&amp;C requirement in sequential order by the end of their fourth semester, or their enrollment will be blocked for the following semester.</p>
<p>The R&amp;C requirement can be satisfied by any of the courses listed with an "R" before its course number in the online Schedule of Classes. More than a dozen departments offer R&amp;C courses, so be sure to check the Online Schedule of Classes.</p>
<p>Students who arrive at Berkeley not having satisfied the Entry-Level Writing requirement (see above) can satisfy both the Entry-Level Writing requirement and the 1st part of the 2-part R&amp;C requirement by taking CW R1A.</p>
<p>Students who arrive at Berkeley having satisfied the Entry-Level Writing requirement (see above) need only satisfy the R&amp;C requirement. There are 2 parts to the R&amp;C requirement, A and B, and they must be fulfilled in sequence. More than a dozen campus departments offer the R&amp;C sequence. R&amp;C courses are designated with an “R” before the course number in the Schedule of Classes. </p>
<h2><br />Other Requirements<br /> </h2>
<h3>The American Cultures Requirement</h3>
<p>The following College Writing courses fulfill the <a class="external-link" href="http://americancultures.berkeley.edu/" target="_blank">American Cultures Requirement.</a></p>
<p>CW 25AC - Reading in and about US Education Institutions<br />CW 50AC/150AC - Researching Water in the West<br />CW 192AC - Advanced Composition: Community-Based Ethics<br /> </p>
<h3>The Seven-Course Breadth Requirement in Arts and Literature</h3>
<p>The following CW courses count toward the <a class="external-link" href="http://ls-advise.berkeley.edu/requirement/breadth7/al.html" target="_blank">Seven-Course Breadth Requirement in Arts and Literature</a>.</p>
<p>CW N2 - Summer Bridge<br />CW 105 - Intermediate Composition: Finding Your Voice<br />CW 106 - Intermediate Composition: Argument in the Disciplines<br />CW 108 - Advanced Composition: New Media<br />CW 110 - Advanced Composition: Challenging Writing<br />CW 180 - Travel Writing<br /> </p>
<h3>The Creative Writing Minor</h3>
<p>The following class counts toward the Undergraduate Division's <a class="external-link" href="http://creative.ugis.berkeley.edu/requirements" target="_blank">Creative Writing Minor</a>.</p>
<p>CW 130 - Introduction to the Craft of Creative Writing<br /> </p>
<h3>The Education Minor</h3>
<p>The following class counts toward the Undergraduate Division's <a class="external-link" href="http://gse.berkeley.edu/sites/default/files/UME%20Appr%20Courses_0.pdf" target="_blank">Education Minor</a>.</p>
<p>CW 25AC - Reading in and about US Education Institutions</p>
</div>
